<p><b>Princess Leia Organa of Alderaan</b>, later known as <b>General Leia Organa</b>, is a fictional character in the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars"><i>Star Wars</i> franchise</a>, portrayed in films by <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Fisher" title="Carrie Fisher">Carrie Fisher</a>. Introduced in the original <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> film in 1977, Leia is princess of the planet <a href="/wiki/Alderaan" title="Alderaan">Alderaan</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Galactic_Empire_(Star_Wars)" title="Galactic Empire (Star Wars)">Imperial Senate</a> and an agent of the <a href="/wiki/Rebel_Alliance" title="Rebel Alliance">Rebel Alliance</a>. She thwarts the sinister <a href="/wiki/Sith" title="Sith">Sith Lord</a> <a href="/wiki/Darth_Vader" title="Darth Vader">Darth Vader</a> and helps bring about the destruction of the Empire's cataclysmic weapon, the <a href="/wiki/Death_Star" title="Death Star">Death Star</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Empire_Strikes_Back" title="The Empire Strikes Back">The Empire Strikes Back</a></i> (1980), Leia commands a Rebel base and evades Vader as she falls in love with the smuggler <a href="/wiki/Han_Solo" title="Han Solo">Han Solo</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i> (1983), Leia leads the operation to rescue Han from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_lord" title="Crime lord">crime lord</a> <a href="/wiki/Jabba_the_Hutt" title="Jabba the Hutt">Jabba the Hutt</a>, and is revealed to be Vader's daughter and the twin sister of <a href="/wiki/Luke_Skywalker" title="Luke Skywalker">Luke Skywalker</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prequel_trilogy_(Star_Wars)" title="Prequel trilogy (Star Wars)">prequel</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_%E2%80%93_Revenge_of_the_Sith" title="Star Wars: Episode III – Revenge of the Sith">Revenge of the Sith</a></i> (2005) establishes that the twins' mother is Senator (and former queen) <a href="/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala" title="Padmé Amidala">Padmé Amidala</a> of <a href="/wiki/Naboo" title="Naboo">Naboo</a>, who dies after childbirth. Leia is adopted by Senator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bail_Organa" title="Bail Organa">Bail</a> and Queen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breha_Organa" title="Breha Organa">Breha Organa</a> of Alderaan. In <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">The Force Awakens</a></i> (2015), Leia is the founder and General of the Resistance against the <a href="/wiki/First_Order_(Star_Wars)" title="First Order (Star Wars)">First Order</a> and has a son with Han named Ben, who now goes by the name <a href="/wiki/Kylo_Ren" title="Kylo Ren">Kylo Ren</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_expanded_universe" title="Star Wars expanded universe">original <i>Star Wars</i> expanded universe (1977–2014)</a> of novels, comics and video games, which are set in an alternate <a href="/wiki/Continuity_(fiction)" title="Continuity (fiction)">continuity</a>, Leia continues her adventures with Han and Luke after <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, fighting Imperial resurgences and new threats to the galaxy. She becomes the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">Chief of State</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_Republic_(Star_Wars)" title="New Republic (Star Wars)">New Republic</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Jedi" title="Jedi">Jedi Master</a>, and is the mother to three children by Han: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaina_Solo" title="Jaina Solo">Jaina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacen_Solo" title="Jacen Solo">Jacen</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anakin_Solo" title="Anakin Solo">Anakin Solo</a>.</p>
<p>One of the more popular <i>Star Wars</i> characters, Leia has been called a 1980s <a href="/wiki/Cultural_icon" title="Cultural icon">icon</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">feminist</a> hero and model for other adventure heroines. She has appeared in many derivative works and merchandising, and has been referenced or <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parodied</a> in several TV shows and films. Her "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cinnamon_bun" title="Cinnamon bun">cinnamon buns</a>" hairstyle from <i>Star Wars</i> (1977) and <a href="/wiki/Princess_Leia%27s_bikini" title="Princess Leia's bikini">metal bikini</a> from <i>Return of the Jedi</i> have become cultural icons.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_and_casting">Creation and casting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Creation and casting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Leia was created by <i>Star Wars</i> creator <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>. In 1999, Lucas explained his early development of Leia, Luke and <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The first [version] talked about a princess and an old general. The second version involved a father, his son, and his daughter; the daughter was the heroine of the film. Now the daughter has become Luke, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hamill" title="Mark Hamill">Mark Hamill</a>'s character. There was also the story of two brothers where I transformed one of them into a sister. The older brother was imprisoned, and the young sister had to rescue him and bring him back to their dad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Film historian Laurent Bouzereau notes in his 1997 book <i>Star Wars: The Annotated Screenplays</i> that in the rough draft of <i>Star Wars</i>, Leia is the spoiled teenage daughter of King Kayos and Queen Breha of Aquilae, with two brothers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biggs_Darklighter" title="Biggs Darklighter">Biggs</a> and Windy; Biggs returned to the fourth draft as a childhood friend of Luke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> According to <i>Skywalking: The Life and Films of George Lucas</i> (1999), Luke Skywalker was originally Luke Starkiller and Leia was "the daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Owen_Lars" title="Owen Lars">Owen Lars</a> and his wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beru_Lars" title="Beru Lars">Beru</a> and seems to be Luke's cousin–together they visit the grave of his mother, who perished with his father on a planet destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Death_Star" title="Death Star">Death Star</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> J. W. Rinzler explains in <i>The Making of Star Wars: The Definitive Story Behind the Original Film</i> (2007) that a later story synopsis establishes Leia as "Leia Antilles", the daughter of Bail Antilles from the peaceful world of Organa Major. In the fourth draft it was established that "Leia Organa" came instead from Alderaan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Making_of_Star_Wars:_The_Definitive_Story_Behind_the_Original_Film_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Making_of_Star_Wars:_The_Definitive_Story_Behind_the_Original_Film-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fisher was 19 when she was cast as Princess Leia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Melted_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Melted-5">[5]</a></sup> with actresses including <a href="/wiki/Amy_Irving" title="Amy Irving">Amy Irving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cindy_Williams" title="Cindy Williams">Cindy Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jodie_Foster" title="Jodie Foster">Jodie Foster</a> also up for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/InkTank" title="InkTank">InkTank</a> reported that the extended list of "more than two dozen actresses" who had auditioned for Leia included <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Close" title="Glenn Close">Glenn Close</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farrah_Fawcett" title="Farrah Fawcett">Farrah Fawcett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Lange" title="Jessica Lange">Jessica Lange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sissy_Spacek" title="Sissy Spacek">Sissy Spacek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cybill_Shepherd" title="Cybill Shepherd">Cybill Shepherd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Seymour_(actress)" title="Jane Seymour (actress)">Jane Seymour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anjelica_Huston" title="Anjelica Huston">Anjelica Huston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Basinger" title="Kim Basinger">Kim Basinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Turner" title="Kathleen Turner">Kathleen Turner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geena_Davis" title="Geena Davis">Geena Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meryl_Streep" title="Meryl Streep">Meryl Streep</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Asked about Streep in 2015, Fisher said, "Bullshit! I've never heard that one. But Jodie Foster was up for it... that one I knew the most. Amy Irving and Jodie. And I got it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beast_2015_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beast_2015-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second draft of the <i>Return of the Jedi</i> screenplay contained dialogue in which Obi-Wan tells Luke he has a twin sister. She and their mother were "sent to the protection of friends in a distant system. The mother died shortly thereafter, and Luke's sister was adopted by Ben's friends, the governor of Alderaan and his wife."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Fisher explained in 1983: "Leia's real father left her mother when she was pregnant, so her mother married this King Organa. I was adopted and grew up set apart from other people because I was a princess."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_1983_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_1983-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Princess_Leia.27s_Theme"></span>Composer <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> created a musical <a href="/wiki/Leitmotif" title="Leitmotif">leitmotif</a> for Leia which recurs throughout the <i>Star Wars</i> saga. "Princess Leia's Theme" was recorded as a concert suite (4:18 length) for the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(soundtrack)" title="Star Wars (soundtrack)">score of the 1977 film</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Character">Character</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Character">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Anthony Breznican of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> describes Leia as a "diplomat, spy, warrior, undercover agent".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_More_2015_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_More_2015-14">[14]</a></sup> Mark Edlitz calls her "a smart, feisty, brave diplomat and warrior" in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edlitz_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edlitz-15">[15]</a></sup> Fisher told <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> in 1983:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>There are a lot of people who don't like my character in these movies; they think I'm some kind of space bitch. She has no friends, no family; her planet was blown up in seconds ... so all she has is a cause. From the first film [<i>Star Wars</i>], she was just a soldier, front line and center. The only way they knew to make the character strong was to make her angry. In <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, she gets to be more feminine, more supportive, more affectionate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_1983_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_1983-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>She said in 2014:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I would rather have played Han Solo. When I first read the script I thought that's the part to be, always wry and sardonic. He's always that. I feel like a lot of the time Leia's either worried or pissed or, thank God, sort of snarky. But I'm much more worried and pissed than Han Solo ever was, and those aren't fun things to play ... I had a lot of fun killing <a href="/wiki/Jabba_the_Hutt" title="Jabba the Hutt">Jabba the Hutt</a>. They asked me on the day if I wanted to have a stunt double kill Jabba. No! That's the best time I ever had as an actor. And the only reason to go into acting is if you can kill a giant monster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Melted_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Melted-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearances">Appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feature_films">Feature films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Feature films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Wars"><i>Star Wars</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Star Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Introduced in the original 1977 film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i>, Princess Leia Organa of <a href="/wiki/Alderaan" title="Alderaan">Alderaan</a> is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Galactic_Empire_(Star_Wars)" title="Galactic Empire (Star Wars)">Imperial Senate</a>. She is captured by <a href="/wiki/Darth_Vader" title="Darth Vader">Darth Vader</a> on board the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Tantive_IV" title="Tantive IV">Tantive IV</a></i>, where she is acting as a spy for the <a href="/wiki/Rebel_Alliance" title="Rebel Alliance">Rebel Alliance</a>. Leia has secretly hidden the plans for the <a href="/wiki/Death_Star" title="Death Star">Death Star</a>, the Empire's planet-sized battle station, inside the <a href="/wiki/Droid_(robot)" title="Droid (robot)">astromech droid</a> <a href="/wiki/R2-D2" title="R2-D2">R2-D2</a> and has sent it to find one of the last remaining <a href="/wiki/Jedi" title="Jedi">Jedi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a>, on the nearby planet of <a href="/wiki/Tatooine" title="Tatooine">Tatooine</a>. Vader arrests Leia and has her tortured, but she resists revealing anything. Death Star commander <a href="/wiki/Grand_Moff_Tarkin" title="Grand Moff Tarkin">Grand Moff Tarkin</a> threatens to destroy her home planet Alderaan with the Death Star unless she reveals the location of the hidden Rebel base. She provides the location of an old, abandoned base, but Tarkin orders Alderaan to be destroyed anyway. Leia is rescued by Obi-Wan, <a href="/wiki/Luke_Skywalker" title="Luke Skywalker">Luke Skywalker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Han_Solo" title="Han Solo">Han Solo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wookiee" title="Wookiee">Wookiee</a> <a href="/wiki/Chewbacca" title="Chewbacca">Chewbacca</a> and the two droids R2-D2 and <a href="/wiki/C-3PO" title="C-3PO">C-3PO</a>, and they escape aboard Han's ship, the <i><a href="/wiki/Millennium_Falcon" title="Millennium Falcon">Millennium Falcon</a></i>. After analyzing the Death Star's plans, the Rebels find a tiny weakness in the battle station, which Luke uses to destroy it in his <a href="/wiki/X-wing_fighter" title="X-wing fighter">X-wing fighter</a>. The battle won, Leia bestows medals on its heroes at the hidden Rebel base on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yavin_4" title="Yavin 4">Yavin 4</a>.</p>
<p>Alyssa Rosenberg of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> writes of Leia in the film:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Leia’s nerves as a revolutionary are clear from the moment she arrives on screen ... She takes shots at the Storm Troopers boarding her ship, gets stunned with a blaster in her hand, then has the audacity to try to make Darth Vader feel ashamed of himself ... She has enough energy left over after a nasty session of torture to insult Grand Moff Tarkin. And while she grieves when her home planet, Alderaan, is destroyed by the Death Star, Leia’s not paralyzed: when her unexpected rescuers show up, she’s ready to go, and to gripe about their operational sloppiness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Icon_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Icon-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Rosenberg also notes that, though Han is almost immediately attracted to Leia, they conflict because she insists on asserting command and he automatically resists, even as she proves herself to be worthy of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Icon_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Icon-16">[16]</a></sup> And despite her initial disdain for the smuggler, whom she sees as selfish, Leia later acknowledges "I knew there was more to you than money" when Han comes through for the Rebellion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Icon_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Icon-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fisher told <i>Rolling Stone</i> in 1980 that in the original script, when Luke and Han come to rescue a captured Leia, "I was hanging upside down with yellow eyes, like in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Exorcist_(film)" title="The Exorcist (film)">The Exorcist</a></i> ... Some form of radar torture was done to me and I was in a beam, bruised and beaten up, suspended in midair. The reason it was cut from the film was because I was unconscious and the Wookiee would have had to carry me for, like, the next fifteen minutes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_1980_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_1980-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Empire_Strikes_Back"><i>The Empire Strikes Back</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Empire Strikes Back">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Empire_Strikes_Back" title="The Empire Strikes Back">The Empire Strikes Back</a></i> (1980), Leia is at the Rebel base on <a href="/wiki/Hoth" title="Hoth">Hoth</a>. She leads its evacuation during an Imperial attack, and then flees with Han, Chewbacca and C-3PO on Han's ship, the <i><a href="/wiki/Millennium_Falcon" title="Millennium Falcon">Millennium Falcon</a></i>. They dodge pursuing Imperial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TIE_fighters" title="TIE fighters">TIE fighters</a> by flying into an asteroid field when the <i>Falcon</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> hyperdrive breaks down, with Leia piloting the ship at one point. Romance blossoms between Leia and Han during their flight from the Empire; while hiding in the stomach of a space slug, they finally share a kiss. With his ship needing repairs, Han seeks out his old friend <a href="/wiki/Lando_Calrissian" title="Lando Calrissian">Lando Calrissian</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bespin" title="Bespin">Cloud City</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Floating_city_(science_fiction)" title="Floating city (science fiction)">floating city</a> over <a href="/wiki/Bespin" title="Bespin">Bespin</a>. Though he welcomes them graciously, Lando soon turns them over to a newly arrived Darth Vader, who hopes to use them as bait to capture Luke. Leia confesses her love for Han as he is frozen in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbonite_(Star_Wars)" title="Carbonite (Star Wars)">carbonite</a> and then handed over to bounty hunter <a href="/wiki/Boba_Fett" title="Boba Fett">Boba Fett</a>, who is charged with bringing him to gangster <a href="/wiki/Jabba_the_Hutt" title="Jabba the Hutt">Jabba the Hutt</a>. Lando helps Leia, Chewbacca and the two droids escape. Leia senses that Luke is in trouble, and goes back to save him after he is nearly killed during a <a href="/wiki/Lightsaber" title="Lightsaber">lightsaber</a> duel with Vader.</p>
<p>Rosenberg notes:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Yes, it’s slightly ridiculous ... that [Han] tries to pry a confession of affection out of her on Hoth, as Leia is trying to manage an evacuation with just an ion cannon for defense. But Han’s not wrong that if Leia doesn't figure out that she’s a person with needs, she's going to burn out ... In a way, it’s an early confession of love: Han’s anxious about the bounty hunters who are still pursuing him ... But he would stay and give his love and support to Leia if she could just acknowledge that she needs him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Icon_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Icon-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_of_the_Jedi"><i>Return of the Jedi</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Return of the Jedi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i> (1983), Leia infiltrates Jabba's palace on Tatooine disguised as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ubese" title="Ubese">Ubese</a> bounty hunter Boushh, and brings a captive Chewbacca with her as part of the ruse. She frees Han from the carbonite, but they are recaptured by Jabba. Leia is now chained to Jabba as his slave, outfitted in a <a href="/wiki/Princess_Leia%27s_bikini" title="Princess Leia's bikini">metal bikini</a>. After Luke arrives and kills Jabba's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rancor" title="Rancor">Rancor</a>, Jabba sentences Luke, Han and Chewbacca to be fed to the <a href="/wiki/Sarlacc" title="Sarlacc">Sarlacc</a>. Lando (disguised as a guard) helps them overpower their captors, and Leia seizes the moment to strangle Jabba with her chain. Luke and Leia swing to safety, blowing up Jabba's barge behind them. Later, the heroes go to the forest moon of <a href="/wiki/Endor_(Star_Wars)" title="Endor (Star Wars)">Endor</a> to prepare for a battle with the Empire. There, Luke reveals to Leia that she is his twin sister and that Vader is their father. Leia joins Han in leading the Rebels in battle with Imperial troops as the Rebel Fleet attacks the second Death Star. Leia is slightly injured, but the Rebels, with help from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ewoks" title="Ewoks">Ewoks</a>, defeat the forces of the Empire.</p>
<p>Fisher told <i>Rolling Stone</i> in 1983, "In <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, [Leia] gets to be more feminine, more supportive, more affectionate. But let's not forget that these movies are basically boys' fantasies. So the other way they made her more female in this one was to have her take off her clothes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_1983_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_1983-13">[13]</a></sup> Rosenberg writes of Han and Leia:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>And we know those two crazy kids are locked for life in <i>Return of the Jedi</i> when it turns out that Han has accepted a Generalship in the Rebellion, keeping it a secret from Leia. In <i>A New Hope</i>, Leia was grumbling about the quality of Han as a rescuer ... But when she finds out what Han’s done, accepting a rank he once found insulting and a mission she knows to be dangerous, Leia is the first person to volunteer to join his strike team. In <i>Star Wars</i>, that’s what love looks like: trusting your partner’s commitment to the cause and respecting his strategic and technical judgement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Icon_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Icon-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In the film, Leia says that she has vague memories of her real mother, who she describes as "kind... but sad". Bouzereau quoted Lucas in 1997:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The part that I never really developed is the death of Luke and Leia's mother. I had a <a href="/wiki/Backstory" title="Backstory">backstory</a> for her in earlier drafts, but it basically didn't survive. When I got to <i>Jedi</i>, I wanted one of the kids to have some kind of memory of her because she will be a key figure in the new episodes I'm writing. But I really debated whether or not Leia should remember her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenge_of_the_Sith"><i>Revenge of the Sith</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Revenge of the Sith">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Wars_prequel_trilogy" title="Star Wars prequel trilogy">prequel film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_%E2%80%93_Revenge_of_the_Sith" title="Star Wars: Episode III – Revenge of the Sith">Revenge of the Sith</a></i> (2005), <a href="/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala" title="Padmé Amidala">Padmé Amidala</a> is pregnant with Anakin Skywalker's twins near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Clone_Wars_(Star_Wars)" title="Clone Wars (Star Wars)">Clone Wars</a>. After Anakin turns to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_side_(Star_Wars)" title="Dark side (Star Wars)">dark side of the Force</a> and becomes Darth Vader, Padmé gives birth to Luke and Leia on Polis Massa and then dies. Leia is adopted by Senator Bail Organa and his wife Queen Breha of Alderaan.</p>
<p>Film critic <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> of <i>Rolling Stone</i> writes, "As we watch Anakin nearly melt in the lava, only to be put together, <a href="/wiki/Frankenstein" title="Frankenstein">Frankenstein</a> style, in a lab while Lucas intercuts scenes of Padme giving birth to the twins Luke and Leia, a link to genuine feeling is established at last. It's too little and too late. To hail <i>Revenge of the Sith</i> as a satisfying bridge to a classic is not just playing a game of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor%27s_New_Clothes" title="Emperor's New Clothes">Emperor's New Clothes</a></i>, it's an insult to what the original accomplished."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Force_Awakens"><i>The Force Awakens</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Force Awakens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2366" data-file-width="1506" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg/170px-Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg/255px-Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg/340px-Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carrie_Fisher_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Carrie_Fisher" title="Carrie Fisher">Carrie Fisher</a> reprised the role of Leia in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i> in 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2013, Fisher confirmed that she would reprise her role as Leia in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Set 32 years after <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, <i>The Force Awakens</i> reintroduces a Leia who is "a little more battle weary, a little more broken hearted".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_More_2015_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-EW_More_2015-14">[14]</a></sup> In November 2015, director <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.J._Abrams" title="J.J. Abrams">J.J. Abrams</a> said of Leia, "She’s referred to as General but ... there's a moment in the movie where a character sort of slips and calls her 'Princess.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_General_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_General-21">[21]</a></sup> Commenting on the story he added, "The stakes are pretty high in the story for her, so there’s not much goofing around where Leia’s concerned."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_General_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-EW_General-21">[21]</a></sup> Asked how Leia is handling things in the film, Fisher said, "Not easily ... [she is] solitary. Under a lot of pressure. Committed as ever to her cause, but I would imagine feeling somewhat defeated, tired, and pissed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_General_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-EW_General-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the film, Leia is the leader of the Resistance, a group formed by the New Republic to fight a proxy war with the <a href="/wiki/First_Order_(Star_Wars)" title="First Order (Star Wars)">First Order</a> and trying to find Luke, who disappeared years earlier. When her forces foil a First Order attack searching for the Resistance <a href="/wiki/Droid_(robot)" title="Droid (robot)">astromech droid</a> <a href="/wiki/BB-8" title="BB-8">BB-8</a>, Leia is reunited with Han, who has helped the renegade <a href="/wiki/Stormtrooper_(Star_Wars)" title="Stormtrooper (Star Wars)">stormtrooper</a> <a href="/wiki/Finn_(Star_Wars)" title="Finn (Star Wars)">Finn</a> and orphaned scavenger <a href="/wiki/Rey_(Star_Wars)" title="Rey (Star Wars)">Rey</a> bring the droid this far. Han and Leia have been estranged for many years; their marriage fell apart after their son, Ben, fell to the dark side and became the First Order commander <a href="/wiki/Kylo_Ren" title="Kylo Ren">Kylo Ren</a>. Leia believes Ben can still be brought back to the light side. Han volunteers for a mission to infiltrate the First Order's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starkiller_Base" title="Starkiller Base">Starkiller Base</a> to disable its defensive shields. Confronting Ren, Han tries to convince his son to leave the First Order, but Ren instead impales his father on his <a href="/wiki/Lightsaber" title="Lightsaber">lightsaber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Han_Death_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Han_Death-22">[22]</a></sup> Leia senses Han's death through <a href="/wiki/The_Force_(Star_Wars)" title="The Force (Star Wars)">the Force</a>, and later shares a moment of grief with Rey, who had thought of Han as a mentor. Leia sees Rey, Chewbacca, and R2-D2 off when they depart to locate Luke, saying, "may the Force be with you".</p>
<p>Asked why Leia is not shown to be a Jedi in <i>The Force Awakens</i> (as she is in the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_expanded_universe" title="Star Wars expanded universe"><i>Star Wars</i> expanded universe</a> works), Abrams told <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>, "It was a great question, and one that we talked about quite a bit, even with Carrie [Fisher]. Why did she not take advantage of this natural Force strength that this character had. And one of the answers was that it was simply a choice that she made, that her decision to run the Rebellion, and ultimately this Resistance, and consider herself a General, as opposed to a Jedi. It was simply a choice that she took". He also added, "I would like to think that there really isn't much of a ticking clock, and it's never too late ... clearly we've seen, and we do again, that she still is Force strong. And it's something that I think is an intrinsic piece of her character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fisher was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/42nd_Saturn_Awards" title="42nd Saturn Awards">2016 Saturn Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Saturn Award for Best Supporting Actress">Best Supporting Actress</a> for her portrayal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saturn_42_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saturn_42-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Last_Jedi"><i>The Last Jedi</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The Last Jedi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In December 2015, producer <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Kennedy_(producer)" title="Kathleen Kennedy (producer)">Kathleen Kennedy</a> confirmed that Fisher would reprise the role of Leia in the next installment, then known as <i>Star Wars: Episode VIII</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> but later named <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi" title="Star Wars: The Last Jedi">Star Wars: The Last Jedi</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Fisher died on December 27, 2016 after going into cardiac arrest. It was confirmed that she had completed filming her role in the film shortly before her death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_IX"><i>Episode IX</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Episode IX">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following Fisher's death, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> reported that she was slated to appear in <i>Star Wars: Episode IX</i> and speculated that Lucasfilm would need to find a way to address her death and what would become of her character. Filming is expected to begin in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Lucasfilm announced in January 2017 that they had "no plans to digitally recreate Carrie Fisher's performance as Princess or General Leia Organa".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anthology_films">Anthology films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Anthology films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story"><i>Rogue One: A Star Wars Story</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rogue One: A Star Wars Story">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Leia makes a brief appearance in the final scene of the 2016 interquel film <i><a href="/wiki/Rogue_One" title="Rogue One">Rogue One</a></i>, receiving the plans for the Death Star as a lead-up to the beginning of <i>A New Hope</i>. Since this movie takes place prior to the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy, a very young Leia was required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Rogue_One_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Independent_Rogue_One-32">[32]</a></sup> To achieve that effect, a <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated image</a> of a young Carrie Fisher was superimposed over Norwegian actress <a href="/wiki/Ingvild_Deila" title="Ingvild Deila">Ingvild Deila</a>'s face; archival audio of Fisher saying "Hope" was used to voice the character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Rogue_One_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Independent_Rogue_One-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels">Novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Leia makes her first literary appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_From_the_Adventures_of_Luke_Skywalker" title="Star Wars: From the Adventures of Luke Skywalker">Star Wars: From the Adventures of Luke Skywalker</a></i>, the novelization of the original 1977 film <i>Star Wars</i>, which was released six months before the film in November 1976. Credited to Lucas but <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwritten</a> by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dean_Foster" title="Alan Dean Foster">Alan Dean Foster</a>, the novel was based on Lucas' screenplay. Leia later appeared in the novelizations <i><a href="/wiki/The_Empire_Strikes_Back_(novel)" title="The Empire Strikes Back (novel)">The Empire Strikes Back</a></i> (1980) by <a href="/wiki/Donald_F._Glut" title="Donald F. Glut">Donald F. Glut</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi_(novel)" title="Return of the Jedi (novel)">Return of the Jedi</a></i> (1983) by <a href="/wiki/James_Kahn" title="James Kahn">James Kahn</a>. She is also a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-person_limited_narrative" title="Third-person limited narrative">point of view</a> character in the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(novel)" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens (novel)">2015 novelization</a> of <i>The Force Awakens</i> by Foster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FA_novel_I_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FA_novel_I-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Foster's 1978 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Splinter_of_the_Mind%27s_Eye" title="Splinter of the Mind's Eye">Splinter of the Mind's Eye</a></i> was commissioned by Lucas as the basis for a potential low-budget sequel to <i>Star Wars</i> should the film prove unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fry_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-fry-36">[36]</a></sup> In the story, Luke and Leia seek a crystal on a swampy planet and eventually face Vader in combat.</p>
<p>Leia also appears in the <a href="/wiki/Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Journey to Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Journey to <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i></a> line of novels and comic books, introduced in conjunction with <i>The Force Awakens</i> to connect the film with previous installments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Journey_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Journey-37">[37]</a></sup> She is the lead character in the young adult novel <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moving_Target:_A_Princess_Leia_Adventure" title="Moving Target: A Princess Leia Adventure">Moving Target: A Princess Leia Adventure</a></i> (2015) by <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Castellucci" title="Cecil Castellucci">Cecil Castellucci</a> and Jason Fry, which is set between <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i> and <i>Return of the Jedi</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFS_Target_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFS_Target-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deseret_Target_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deseret_Target-39">[39]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Gray" title="Claudia Gray">Claudia Gray</a>'s 2016 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Bloodline" title="Star Wars: Bloodline">Star Wars: Bloodline</a></i>, set several years before <i>The Force Awakens</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UT_Bloodline_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-UT_Bloodline-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tor_Bloodline_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tor_Bloodline-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics">Comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Also part of Journey to <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> are the five-part comic limited series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Princess_Leia" title="Star Wars: Princess Leia">Star Wars: Princess Leia</a></i> (2015), set between <i>Episode IV: A New Hope</i> and <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i>, and the four-part comic limited series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Shattered_Empire" title="Star Wars: Shattered Empire">Star Wars: Shattered Empire</a></i> (2015), set immediately after <i>Return of the Jedi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In <i>Princess Leia</i> #2 and <i>Shattered Empire</i>, Leia is seen using her Force sensitivities to sense the past,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PL_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-PL-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SE_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-SE-44">[44]</a></sup> and in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(2015_comic)" title="Star Wars (2015 comic)">Star Wars</a></i> #12, she uses a lightsaber as a weapon for the first time canonically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> <i>Princess Leia</i> reveals Leia to have had royal training in martial arts and explores her reaction to the destruction of Alderaan, while <i>Shattered Empire</i> also portrays her as a skilled pilot who undertakes a dangerous mission alongside <a href="/wiki/Poe_Dameron" title="Poe Dameron">Poe Dameron</a>'s mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PL_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-PL-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SE_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-SE-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Wars_Holiday_Special"><i>Star Wars Holiday Special</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Star Wars Holiday Special">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Leia appears briefly in the 1978 <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Holiday_Special" title="Star Wars Holiday Special">Star Wars Holiday Special</a></i> TV film as a leader and administrator of the new Rebel Alliance base. She and C-3PO contact Chewbacca's wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mallatobuck" title="Mallatobuck">Mallatobuck</a> for assistance in finding Chewbacca and Han. Leia also appears in the cartoon segment at a different Rebel Base, located in an asteroid field, and at the Life Day ceremony at the end of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Fisher also appeared in and hosted the November 18, 1978 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> that aired one day after the holiday special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The Summer 1983 issue of <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine poked fun at this appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_Covers_RS_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-SW_Covers_RS-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_1983_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_1983-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Wars_Rebels"><i>Star Wars Rebels</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Star Wars Rebels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A teenage version of Princess Leia, voiced by Julie Dolan, appears in a 2016 episode of the <a href="/wiki/Animated_series" title="Animated series">animated series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels" title="Star Wars Rebels">Star Wars Rebels</a></i>, which is set between <i>Revenge of the Sith</i> and <i>A New Hope</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_Insider_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Insider-50">[50]</a></sup> In the episode, Leia is sent on a secret mission to assist the titular rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_Insider_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Insider-50">[50]</a></sup> Executive producer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Filoni" title="Dave Filoni">Dave Filoni</a> said of the appearance:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We thought we had an opportunity to show her learning to be a leader, experimenting with the personality that becomes the stronger more resolute character you see in <i>A New Hope</i>. One of the complex challenges of depicting Leia in <i>Rebels</i> is that we have to remind the audience that at this point she is part of the Empire. She doesn't believe in the Empire, but she is acting the part, almost a double agent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_Insider_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Insider-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legends_works"><i>Legends</i> works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Legends works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_expanded_universe" title="Star Wars expanded universe">Star Wars expanded universe</a></div>
<p>The original three <i>Star Wars</i> films have spawned a large franchise of works that include novels, comic books, video games and animated television series. Leia appears in much of this material. In April 2014 (with the sequel film <i>The Force Awakens</i> in production), <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a> separated the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_expanded_universe" title="Star Wars expanded universe"><i>Star Wars</i> expanded universe</a> (rebranded as <i>Star Wars Legends</i>) from official <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_canon" title="Star Wars canon"><i>Star Wars</i> canon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels_2">Novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 1991 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_List" title="The New York Times Best Seller List"><i>New York Times</i> bestselling</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/Heir_to_the_Empire" title="Heir to the Empire">Heir to the Empire</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Zahn" title="Timothy Zahn">Timothy Zahn</a> began what would become a large collection of works set before, between and especially after the original films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_Heir_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-SW_Heir-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Return_of_the_Jedi">Post-<i>Return of the Jedi</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Post-Return of the Jedi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The bestselling <a href="/wiki/Thrawn_trilogy" title="Thrawn trilogy"><i>Thrawn</i> trilogy</a> (1991–93) by Timothy Zahn begins five years after the events of <i>Return of the Jedi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_Heir_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-SW_Heir-52">[52]</a></sup> In <i>Heir to the Empire</i> (1991), Leia is married to Han and three months pregnant with twins. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noghri" title="Noghri">Noghri</a> commandos repeatedly attempt to kidnap her as part of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Admiral_Thrawn" title="Grand Admiral Thrawn">Grand Admiral Thrawn</a>'s plan to restore the Empire and crush the New Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heir_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-heir-53">[53]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Force_Rising" title="Dark Force Rising">Dark Force Rising</a></i> (1992), Leia realizes that Darth Vader and the Empire deceived the Noghri to secure their allegiance, and by revealing the truth she turns the alien race to the side of the New Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dark_rising_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-dark_rising-54">[54]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Command_(novel)" title="The Last Command (novel)">The Last Command</a></i> (1993), Leia gives birth to the twins <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaina_Solo" title="Jaina Solo">Jaina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacen_Solo" title="Jacen Solo">Jacen</a> on <a href="/wiki/Coruscant" title="Coruscant">Coruscant</a> during Thrawn's siege.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-command_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-command-55">[55]</a></sup> Leia, now the Chief of State of the New Republic, is a minor character in the <a href="/wiki/Jedi_Academy_trilogy" title="Jedi Academy trilogy"><i>Jedi Academy</i> trilogy</a> (1994) by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_J._Anderson" title="Kevin J. Anderson">Kevin J. Anderson</a>, set after the <i>Thrawn</i> trilogy. Next in the timeline is the <i>Callista</i> trilogy: <i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_the_Jedi" title="Children of the Jedi">Children of the Jedi</a></i> (1995) by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly">Barbara Hambly</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darksaber_(novel)" title="Darksaber (novel)">Darksaber</a></i> (1995) by Anderson and <i><a href="/wiki/Planet_of_Twilight" title="Planet of Twilight">Planet of Twilight</a></i> (1997) by Hambly. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crystal_Star" title="The Crystal Star">The Crystal Star</a></i> (1994) by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vonda_McIntyre" title="Vonda McIntyre">Vonda McIntyre</a>, young Jacen, Jaina and their three-year-old brother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anakin_Solo" title="Anakin Solo">Anakin</a> are kidnapped in a plot to restore the Empire, but are rescued by Leia and Chewbacca. Leia struggles with the responsibilities of her position in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Fleet_Crisis" title="The Black Fleet Crisis">The Black Fleet Crisis</a></i> trilogy (1996) by <a href="/wiki/Michael_P._Kube-McDowell" title="Michael P. Kube-McDowell">Michael P. Kube-McDowell</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Rebellion" title="The New Rebellion">The New Rebellion</a></i> (1996) by <a href="/wiki/Kristine_Kathryn_Rusch" title="Kristine Kathryn Rusch">Kristine Kathryn Rusch</a>, she avoids an assassination attempt and then aids in the defeat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_Jedi" title="Dark Jedi">Dark Jedi</a> Kueller, whom she shoots to death. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Corellian_trilogy" title="The Corellian trilogy">The <i>Corellian</i> trilogy</a> (1995) by <a href="/wiki/Roger_MacBride_Allen" title="Roger MacBride Allen">Roger MacBride Allen</a> finds Han and Leia swept up in a civil war while visiting his homeworld of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corellia" title="Corellia">Corellia</a> with their children. In the two <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hand_of_Thrawn" title="The Hand of Thrawn">Hand of Thrawn</a></i> novels by Timothy Zahn (1997's <i><a href="/wiki/Specter_of_the_Past" title="Specter of the Past">Specter of the Past</a></i> and 1998's <i><a href="/wiki/Vision_of_the_Future" title="Vision of the Future">Vision of the Future</a></i>), Leia tries to hold the New Republic together as Moff Disra conspires for its volatile factions to destroy each other. Leia appears periodically in the <i><a href="/wiki/Young_Jedi_Knights" title="Young Jedi Knights">Young Jedi Knights</a></i> series (1995–98) by Kevin J. Anderson and <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Moesta" title="Rebecca Moesta">Rebecca Moesta</a>. The 14-volume <a href="/wiki/Young_adult_fiction" title="Young adult fiction">young adult fiction</a> series covers the Jedi training of Jacen and Jaina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_Jacen_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR_Jacen-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_Jacen_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slate_Jacen-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ScreenRant_Jacen_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ScreenRant_Jacen-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenofGeek_Jacen_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-DenofGeek_Jacen-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Truce_at_Bakura" title="The Truce at Bakura">The Truce at Bakura</a></i> (1993) by <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Tyers" title="Kathy Tyers">Kathy Tyers</a>, set one day after the ending of <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, Leia establishes New Alderaan, a sanctuary for the destroyed planet's surviving inhabitants. The spirit of Anakin Skywalker appears to Leia and pleads for her forgiveness, but she angrily banishes him. The six-volume <a href="/wiki/Jedi_Prince_series" title="Jedi Prince series"><i>Jedi Prince</i> series</a> (1992–93) by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Davids" title="Paul Davids">Paul Davids</a> and Hollace Davids, later contradicted by other novels, is set within a year after <i>Return of the Jedi</i>. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Glove_of_Darth_Vader" title="The Glove of Darth Vader">The Glove of Darth Vader</a></i> (1992), the self-proclaimed son of the defeated Emperor <a href="/wiki/Palpatine" title="Palpatine">Palpatine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trioculus" title="Trioculus">Trioculus</a>, seeks the titular glove to cement himself as the new Emperor. Entranced by Leia's beauty in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_City_of_the_Jedi" title="The Lost City of the Jedi">The Lost City of the Jedi</a></i> (1992), Trioculus vows to make her his queen. He captures her in <i><a href="/wiki/Zorba_the_Hutt%27s_Revenge" title="Zorba the Hutt's Revenge">Zorba the Hutt's Revenge</a></i> (1992), but Jabba the Hutt's vengeful father, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zorba_the_Hutt" title="Zorba the Hutt">Zorba</a>, offers to trade his own prisoner <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ken_(Star_Wars)" title="Ken (Star Wars)">Ken</a>—Palpatine's real grandson whom Trioculus has been seeking—for Leia, his son's killer. But Leia and Ken are rescued and Trioculus is frozen in carbonate by Zorba. <i><a href="/wiki/Mission_from_Mount_Yoda" title="Mission from Mount Yoda">Mission from Mount Yoda</a></i> (1993) finds Ken's father <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triclops_(Star_Wars)" title="Triclops (Star Wars)">Triclops</a> alive and willing to join the Rebels against the Empire. Leia, now engaged to Han, is captured by Zorba in <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_of_the_Empire" title="Queen of the Empire">Queen of the Empire</a></i> (1993). Trioculus is revived and seizes Leia before Zorba can kill her. Leia is rescued and replaced with a lookalike droid decoy, which kills Trioculus. In <i><a href="/wiki/Prophets_of_the_Dark_Side" title="Prophets of the Dark Side">Prophets of the Dark Side</a></i> (1993), Leia looks forward to her wedding to Han and has a vision of their two children. <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Stover" title="Matthew Stover">Matthew Stover</a>'s 2008 standalone novel <i><a href="/wiki/Luke_Skywalker_and_the_Shadows_of_Mindor" title="Luke Skywalker and the Shadows of Mindor">Luke Skywalker and the Shadows of Mindor</a></i> picks up the story soon after, as Luke, Leia and the Rebels fight the <a href="/wiki/Sith" title="Sith">Sith</a> Lord Shadowspawn.</p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Courtship_of_Princess_Leia" title="The Courtship of Princess Leia">The Courtship of Princess Leia</a></i> (1994) by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Wolverton" title="Dave Wolverton">Dave Wolverton</a>, set immediately before the <i>Thrawn</i> trilogy, Leia is presented with an advantageous political marriage to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Isolder" title="Prince Isolder">Prince Isolder</a> of the planet Hapes. A jealous Han abducts Leia and takes her to the planet Dathomir; Luke and Isolder follow, and there they all find the hidden forces of the Imperial warlord Zsinj.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Defeating him, Han and Leia marry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The 2003 novels <i><a href="/wiki/A_Forest_Apart" title="A Forest Apart">A Forest Apart</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tatooine_Ghost" title="Tatooine Ghost">Tatooine Ghost</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Troy_Denning" title="Troy Denning">Troy Denning</a> are set immediately after <i>The Courtship of Princess Leia</i>. The newly married Leia fears that any children she has may succumb to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_side_(Star_Wars)" title="Dark side (Star Wars)">dark side</a> like her father. During an adventure on <a href="/wiki/Tatooine" title="Tatooine">Tatooine</a> in <i>Tatooine Ghost</i>, she discovers the diary of her grandmother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shmi_Skywalker" title="Shmi Skywalker">Shmi Skywalker</a> and meets some of young Anakin's childhood friends. When she learns of Anakin's childhood as a slave and the traumatic death of his mother, Leia learns to forgive her father.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Works_set_between_films">Works set between films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Works set between films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shadows_of_the_Empire_(novel)" title="Shadows of the Empire (novel)">Shadows of the Empire</a></i> (1996) by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Perry_(author)" title="Steve Perry (author)">Steve Perry</a>, the only <i>Star Wars</i> novel set between <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i> and <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, Leia is searching for Boba Fett to find a captive Han. She is bewitched by the crime lord <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Xizor" title="Prince Xizor">Prince Xizor</a> using pheromones, but Chewbacca helps her elude the seduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shadows_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shadows-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Allegiance_(novel)" title="Allegiance (novel)">Allegiance</a></i> (2007) and <i>Choices of One</i> (2011) by Timothy Zahn are set between <i>Star Wars: A New Hope</i> and <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i>, and feature Leia and her cohorts seeking new allies for their Rebellion against the Empire. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_and_Rebellion:_Razor%27s_Edge" title="Empire and Rebellion: Razor's Edge">Razor's Edge</a></i> (2013) by <a href="/wiki/Martha_Wells" title="Martha Wells">Martha Wells</a> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_and_Rebellion:_Honor_Among_Thieves" title="Empire and Rebellion: Honor Among Thieves">Honor Among Thieves</a></i> (2014) by <a href="/wiki/James_S._A._Corey" title="James S. A. Corey">James S. A. Corey</a> take place in the same time period and also chronicle the adventures of Leia and Han.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jedi_Order"><i>New Jedi Order</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: New Jedi Order">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jedi_Order" title="New Jedi Order">New Jedi Order</a></i> series (1999–2003), Leia resigns as Chief of State, and on the heels of her warnings before the Senate, the alien <a href="/wiki/Yuuzhan_Vong" title="Yuuzhan Vong">Yuuzhan Vong</a> invade the galaxy. They destroy system after system and defeat both the Jedi and the New Republic forces in countless battles. Chewbacca dies in <i><a href="/wiki/Vector_Prime" title="Vector Prime">Vector Prime</a></i> (1999) by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R.A._Salvatore" title="R.A. Salvatore">R.A. Salvatore</a>, which sends Han into a deep depression that causes a rift between him and Leia. They reunite after Leia is gravely wounded at the Battle of Duro in Kathy Tyers' <i><a href="/wiki/Balance_Point" title="Balance Point">Balance Point</a></i> (2000). She is targeted by a deadly Voxyn slayer in Troy Dennings' <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_By_Star" title="Star By Star">Star By Star</a></i> (2001), and though she manages to evade death, her son Anakin is later killed during a mission to prevent more Voxyn from being cloned. The Vong are finally defeated in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Unifying_Force" title="The Unifying Force">The Unifying Force</a></i> (2003) by <a href="/wiki/James_Luceno" title="James Luceno">James Luceno</a>.</p>
<p>In Denning's <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Nest_trilogy" title="The Dark Nest trilogy">The <i>Dark Nest</i> trilogy</a> (2005), Leia, Han and several Jedi become involved in an escalating border dispute between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chiss" title="Chiss">Chiss</a> and the insidious insectoid Killiks, and Leia makes a bitter enemy in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twi%27lek" title="Twi'lek">Twi'lek</a> warrior <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alema_Rar" title="Alema Rar">Alema Rar</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Joiner_King" title="The Joiner King">The Joiner King</a></i> (2005), Leia asks <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saba_Sebatyne" title="Saba Sebatyne">Saba Sebatyne</a> to train her as a Jedi Knight. R2-D2 malfunctions in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Unseen_Queen" title="The Unseen Queen">The Unseen Queen</a></i> (2005) and shows Luke a holoclip of his father Anakin and a pregnant woman, whom Luke learns is his and Leia's biological mother, Padmé Amidala. Anakin and Padmé are discussing a dream of Anakin's in which Padmé dies in childbirth; later, Luke and Leia watch a clip in which Padmé is talking to Obi-Wan Kenobi about Anakin. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenel_Ka" title="Tenel Ka">Tenel Ka</a>, Queen Mother of the Hapes Consortium, has a daughter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allana_Solo" title="Allana Solo">Allana</a>, secretly fathered by Jacen. In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Swarm_War" title="The Swarm War">The Swarm War</a></i> (2005), Luke and Leia view holoclips of their mother's death, and Leia is promoted to Jedi Knight.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_of_the_Force"><i>Legacy of the Force</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Legacy of the Force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The bestselling <i><a href="/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Force" title="Legacy of the Force">Legacy of the Force</a></i> series (2006–08) chronicles the crossover of Han and Leia's son Jacen to the dark side of the Force while the Jedi, Solos and Skywalkers fight against his growing power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_Jacen_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-THR_Jacen-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_Jacen_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Slate_Jacen-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ScreenRant_Jacen_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ScreenRant_Jacen-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DenofGeek_Jacen_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-DenofGeek_Jacen-59">[59]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Betrayal_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Betrayal (Star Wars novel)">Betrayal</a></i> (2006) by <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Allston" title="Aaron Allston">Aaron Allston</a>, Jacen turns to the dark side, believing that it is the only way to save the galaxy from the chaos brewing among the member systems of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galactic_Alliance" title="Galactic Alliance">Galactic Alliance</a>. Jacen realizes in <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodlines_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Bloodlines (Star Wars novel)">Bloodlines</a></i> (2006) by <a href="/wiki/Karen_Traviss" title="Karen Traviss">Karen Traviss</a> that the Sith discipline will require him to kill one of his loved ones, which he decides is an acceptable sacrifice to save the galaxy. In Troy Denning's <i><a href="/wiki/Tempest_(novel)" title="Tempest (novel)">Tempest</a></i> (2006), Han and Leia thwart the assassination of Tenel Ka and Allana, but become caught up in a Corellian conspiracy. They are almost killed when the <i>Millennium Falcon</i> is attacked by a <a href="/wiki/Star_Destroyer" title="Star Destroyer">Star Destroyer</a> controlled by an increasingly powerful Jacen—who knows that his parents are on board. With Han injured, Leia and Lando further investigate the Corellians in Aaron Allston's <i><a href="/wiki/Exile_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Exile (Star Wars novel)">Exile</a></i> (2007), but Alema reappears to exact her vengeance on Leia. <i><a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_(novel)" title="Sacrifice (novel)">Sacrifice</a></i> (2007) by Karen Traviss finds Leia and Han on the run, hunted by Jacen as traitors to the Galactic Alliance. He kills Luke's wife <a href="/wiki/Mara_Jade" title="Mara Jade">Mara Jade</a> as his final sacrifice to become Darth Caedus, the new ruler of the Sith. In <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Inferno (Star Wars novel)">Inferno</a></i> (2007) by Troy Denning, Han and Leia are faced with the reality that their son, now Joint Chief of State, is the enemy. Leia attempts unsuccessfully to manipulate Jacen in Aaron Allston's <i><a href="/wiki/Fury_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Fury (Star Wars novel)">Fury</a></i> (2007) so that the Jedi can both thwart him and neutralize Alema. Finally, in <i><a href="/wiki/Invincible_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Invincible (Star Wars novel)">Invincible</a></i> (2008) by Troy Denning, Jaina kills Jacen in lightsaber duel. At Tenel Ka's request, Leia and Han adopt Allana, disguised with the name "Amelia" to protect her from any future vengeance against Cadeus or the Hapes Consortium. Multiple novels in the series made the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_List" title="The New York Times Best Seller List"><i>New York Times</i> Best Seller List</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The nine-volume <i>Fate of the Jedi</i> series (2009–12) by Aaron Allston, Troy Denning and <a href="/wiki/Christie_Golden" title="Christie Golden">Christie Golden</a> finds Han and Leia become caught up in the intensifying conflict between the Galactic Alliance and the Jedi. In the wake of Darth Cadeus' death, the now-peaceful Galactic Alliance harbors a growing mistrust toward the Jedi, and the situation is worsened by a Force-induced psychosis that begins afflicting individual Jedi, sending them on violent rampages.</p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Millennium_Falcon_(novel)" title="Millennium Falcon (novel)">Millennium Falcon</a></i> (2008) by James Luceno, set between <i>Legacy of the Force</i> and <i>Fate of the Jedi</i>, a mysterious device hidden inside the eponymous spacecraft sends Han, Leia and Allana on an adventure to investigate the ship's past before it came into Han's possession. Troy Denning's <i><a href="/wiki/Crucible_(Star_Wars_novel)" title="Crucible (Star Wars novel)">Crucible</a></i> (2013), set after <i>Fate of the Jedi</i> and the last novel to date in the <i>Star Wars Legends</i> chronology, reunites Leia, Han and Luke with Lando as they aid him to thwart a vast criminal enterprise threatening his asteroid mineral refinery in the Chilean Rift <a href="/wiki/Nebula" title="Nebula">nebula</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics_2">Comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_Empire"><i>Dark Empire</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Dark Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>During the events of the comic series <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Empire" title="Dark Empire">Dark Empire</a></i> (1991–92), Palpatine has been resurrected in a young clone body and seduces Luke to the dark side of the Force as part of his plan to restore the Empire. A captive Leia, resisting Palpatine's attempts to turn her as well, escapes with an artifact he needs to secure his power, the Jedi <a href="/wiki/Holocron" title="Holocron">Holocron</a>. Luke pursues her, and Leia manages to turn him back. Brother and sister then fight Palpatine with the light side of the Force, turning his own Force-generated storm against him and destroying Palpatine and his <a href="/wiki/Star_Destroyer" title="Star Destroyer">Star Destroyer</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Empire_II" title="Dark Empire II">Dark Empire II</a></i> (1994–95), Leia gives birth to a third child by Han, whom she names <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anakin_Solo" title="Anakin Solo">Anakin</a>. Palpatine is reborn in an inferior, rapidly deteriorating clone body in <i><a href="/wiki/Empire%27s_End" title="Empire's End">Empire's End</a></i> (1995), and seeks to possess the body of the infant Anakin.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cultural impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_(17176977836).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg/220px-SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg/330px-SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg/440px-SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_%2817176977836%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SWCA_-_Princess_Leia_(17176977836).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Leia <a href="/wiki/Cosplay" title="Cosplay">cosplay</a> (<a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Celebration" title="Star Wars Celebration"><i>Star Wars</i> Celebration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>, April 2015)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Princess Leia has been called a 1980s icon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_Schou_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_Schou-68">[68]</a></sup> a feminist hero<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Bikini_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Bikini-69">[69]</a></sup> and "an exemplary personification of female empowerment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edlitz_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edlitz-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2008, Leia was selected by <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine as the 89th greatest film character of all time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Empire_89_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Empire_89-70">[70]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> listed her as their 8th top <i>Star Wars</i> hero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopHero_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-TopHero-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UGO_Networks" title="UGO Networks">UGO Networks</a> listed Leia as one of their best heroes of all time in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UGO_Heroes_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-UGO_Heroes-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The character has been referenced or <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parodied</a> in several TV shows and films,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_Film.2BTV_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_Film.2BTV-73">[73]</a></sup> and celebrated in <a href="/wiki/Cosplay" title="Cosplay">cosplay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Fisher appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Princess_Leia%27s_bikini" title="Princess Leia's bikini">Leia metal bikini</a> on the cover of the Summer 1983 issue of <i>Rolling Stone</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SW_Covers_RS_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-SW_Covers_RS-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_1983_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-RS_1983-49">[49]</a></sup> and a painting of Leia and other characters surrounding Lucas appeared on the cover of the May 25, 1983 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> announcing <i>Return of the Jedi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> In 2013, cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Brown_(cartoonist)" title="Jeffrey Brown (cartoonist)">Jeffrey Brown</a> published the bestselling <i>Star Wars: Vader's Little Princess</i>, a comic strip-style book featuring Darth Vader and a young Leia in humorous father-daughter situations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Princess Leia appears on a 2007 US postage stamp<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and a 2015 UK stamp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leia has also been used in a wide range of <i>Star Wars</i> merchandise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daily_Beast_2011_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Beast_2011-85">[85]</a></sup> including statuettes, action figures and other toys, household items and clothing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blastr_Merch_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blastr_Merch-86">[86]</a></sup> office supplies, food products,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWCA_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-SWCA-87">[87]</a></sup> and bubble bath and shampoo in Leia-shaped bottles with her head as the cap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsweek_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In her one-woman show <i><a href="/wiki/Wishful_Drinking" title="Wishful Drinking">Wishful Drinking</a></i>, Fisher called the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Pez" title="Star Wars Pez">Princess Leia Pez dispenser</a> one of the "merchandising horrors" of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In a 2011 interview, Fisher said:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I signed away my likeness for free. In those days, there was no such thing as a “likeness" ... There was no merchandising tied to movies. No one could have known the extent of the franchise. Not that I don’t think I’m cute or anything, but when I looked in the mirror, I didn’t think I was signing away anything of value. Lately I feel like I’m <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Mouse" title="Minnie Mouse">Minnie Mouse</a>—the identity of Princess Leia so eclipses any other identity that I’ve ever had.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daily_Beast_2011_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Beast_2011-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>After the 2012 acquisition of LucasFilm by the Walt Disney Company, the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Store" title="Disney Store">Disney Store</a> stated in May 2014 that the company had "no plans for Leia products".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_2014_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time_2014-92">[92]</a></sup> After public criticism, Disney told <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> in June 2014 that it would be releasing several Leia products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_2014_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time_2014-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Funko" title="Funko">Funko</a> has since produced several versions of Leia (at least one for each film) in their POP! line of 4.5 inch vinyl figures in the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Super_deformed" title="Super deformed">super deformed</a> style. <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a> is set to release an action figure of Leia as she appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels" title="Star Wars Rebels">Star Wars Rebels</a></i> animated series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Cinnamon_buns.22_hairstyle">"Cinnamon buns" hairstyle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Leia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title='Edit section: "Cinnamon buns" hairstyle'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:194px;max-width:194px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:220px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="731" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg/192px-Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg/288px-Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg/384px-Edward_S._Curtis_Collection_People_043.jpg 2x" width="192"/></a></div>
